## Phase 5a: Infrastructure Cleanup + Foundation Utilities (~1-2 sessions)

**Goal:** Clean up temporary/eval code, extract commands, add foundational utilities (yielding, debug logging, app store, settings migration), set up ESLint, and restructure stores for the remaining phases. No new user-facing features ŌĆö this is pure infrastructure.

### Pre-Phase Entry Checks (must already be true before starting 5a)

- [x] You're on the correct git branch
- [x] You've reviewed the current `main.ts`, `src/views/`, and `src/constants.ts` to understand the current state
- [x] Run the Async Promise Handling Gate grep (see Plan-Wide Rules) ŌĆö identify any unhandled async patterns

### Mandatory First Tasks (items 0-3 below ŌĆö MUST complete before any other 5a items)

These cleanup tasks must be done first so that the ESLint gate (item 4) and the innerHTML grep gate don't fail on existing violations. After completing items 0-3, run:
```
grep -rn "innerHTML\|outerHTML\|insertAdjacentHTML\|UPlotEvalView\|ChartJsEvalView\|HINDSIGHT_UPLOT\|CHARTJS_EVAL" src/ main.ts
```
Expected: zero results. Only then proceed to item 4+.
 **Fail-fast (A24):** If any eval artifact (`UPlotEvalView`, `ChartJsEvalView`, `innerHTML`) exists after items 0-3, Phase 5b+ work is NOT allowed to start. Eval view deletion must be the absolute first action in Phase 5a ŌĆö these are dead code deletions, not code fixes, so there is no reason to defer them.

### Pre-Phase Cleanup (MUST complete before any new code)

0. **Fix unhandled promises in `settings.ts` AND file watcher handlers:** Wrap all async event listener callbacks with proper promise handling. Every `addEventListener('blur', async () => { ... })` must use the `void` operator or `.catch(console.error)` pattern. Additionally, wrap `JournalIndexService` file watcher handler bodies in try/catch ŌĆö currently, errors thrown inside `setTimeout(async () => ŌĆ”)` and `vault.on('create', async () => ŌĆ”)` are silently swallowed:
    ```typescript
    // Pattern for setTimeout async handlers:
    setTimeout(() => {
        void (async () => {
            try {
                // ...existing handler logic...
            } catch (err) {
                console.error('[Hindsight] File watcher error:', err);
            }
        })();
    }, DEBOUNCE_MS);
    ```
    This is the #1 most-flagged issue in Obsidian plugin reviews and must be resolved before the ESLint `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises: "error"` rule is added (item 17), or the build will immediately fail on existing violations. Apply the same fix to all async `onChange` callbacks.
1. **Remove uPlot:** `npm uninstall uplot`. Delete `src/views/UPlotEvalView.ts`. Remove `HINDSIGHT_UPLOT_EVAL_VIEW_TYPE` from `src/constants.ts`. Remove the uPlot view registration and command from `main.ts`. **Verify file extension:** the actual file is `.ts` (not `.tsx`) ŌĆö confirm with `ls src/views/UPlot*` before deleting. **SECURITY GATE:** This file contains `innerHTML` usage (line 155: `tooltipEl.innerHTML = html`) which is a [BLOCKER] per Obsidian guidelines ŌĆö the review bot auto-flags every instance. This deletion is a security requirement, not optional cleanup.
2. **Remove Chart.js eval view:** Delete `src/views/ChartJsEvalView.ts`. Remove `CHARTJS_EVAL_VIEW_TYPE` from `src/constants.ts`. Remove the Chart.js eval view registration and command from `main.ts`. **Verify file extension:** confirm actual extension with `ls src/views/ChartJs*`. **SECURITY GATE:** Same as item 1 ŌĆö eval views were temporary experiments and must be deleted before ESLint is enabled.
3. **Remove debug-index command:** Delete the `debug-index` command block from `main.ts`.
 **Strict verification (amendment):** The zero-result grep outputs for eval/debug artifact removal must be a mandatory artifact before Phase 5a continues past items 0-3. All eval commands, debug commands, console.debug calls, and innerHTML usage must produce zero grep results before proceeding.
4. **Extract commands to `src/commands.ts`:** Move all `addCommand()` calls from `main.ts` into a `registerCommands(plugin: HindsightPlugin)` function. `main.ts` calls `registerCommands(this)` in `onload()`. This keeps main.ts under ~100 lines.
5. **Create `src/utils/yieldUtils.ts` (FOUNDATION UTILITY ŌĆö do this before items 6-18):** Shared `processWithYielding()` utility for time-based main-thread yielding with `sync` and `signal` options (see Plan-Wide Rules "Time-Based Yielding" and "Cancellation Support"). Refactor `JournalIndexService.runPass2()` to use it instead of the current fixed 50-file batching. This is the most performance-critical change in the entire plan ŌĆö it directly affects mobile users where fixed batch sizes cause dropped frames. Every subsequent phase that adds background processing (correlation computation, full-text search, annotation migration, thumbnail generation) depends on this utility.
6. **Add `debugMode` setting:** Add `debugMode: boolean` (default `false`) to `HindsightSettings` and `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`. Add it to the settings tab under a new "Advanced" collapsed section. Create `src/utils/debugLog.ts` with the shared `debugLog()` helper. Replace ALL `console.debug` calls across the ENTIRE codebase (not just `main.ts`) with `debugLog()` calls. Run `grep -rn 'console.debug' src/ main.ts` to find all instances ŌĆö `JournalIndexService.ts` also has debug statements from Phase 1 that need conversion.
7. **Create `src/store/appStore.ts`:** Zustand store for `App` and `HindsightPluginInterface` singletons (see Plan-Wide Rules "App/Plugin Access"). Define `HindsightPluginInterface` in `src/types/plugin.ts` to avoid circular imports with `main.ts`. Add `isUnloading: boolean` flag (default `false`). Initialize in `main.ts onload()` with `useAppStore.getState().setApp(this.app, this)`. Refactor existing components (`EchoCard`, `CalendarCell`, `TimelineList`, `JournalIndex`, etc.) to use `const app = useAppStore(s => s.app); if (!app) return null;` ŌĆö **never use `!` non-null assertion on `app` or `plugin`** (see Plan-Wide Rules "App/Plugin Access"). No context providers or view shell changes needed.
8. **Add store reset actions:** Add `reset()` actions to `journalStore`, `uiStore`, `settingsStore`, and `appStore`. Update `onunload()` in `main.ts` to call all store resets. See Plan-Wide Rules "Store Lifecycle" section.
9. **Debounce `detectFields()`:** In `JournalIndexService`, replace the per-event `detectFields()` calls in all file watcher handlers with a single debounced function (5-second delay). Direct `detectFields()` calls remain only in `runPass1()`, `runPass2()`, and `reconfigure()`. When a file watcher event fires, compare the changed entry's frontmatter keys against `detectedFields` keys ŌĆö only set `journalStore.schemaDirty = true` if keys were added or removed (see Plan-Wide Rules "Field Detection Performance" ŌĆö schema-dirty flag). After the debounced `detectFields()` completes, set `schemaDirty = false`. Add `schemaDirty: boolean` (default `false`) and `setSchemaDirty(dirty: boolean)` to `journalStore`.
9a. **Add atomic indexing lock to `JournalIndexService`:** Add `private isIndexing = false` and `private needsReindex = false` flags. If a re-index or `detectFields()` is requested while `isIndexing` is `true`, set `needsReindex = true` and skip. When the current indexing pass completes, check `needsReindex` ŌĆö if `true`, reset it and start one more pass. This prevents overlapping index runs during bulk file operations (git pull, Obsidian Sync, bulk vault modifications).
9b. **Add file watcher bulk event settling mode:** Add settling logic to `FileWatcherService`: if >10 file events fire within 500ms, switch to bulk mode ŌĆö pause individual event processing, wait for events to stop for 2 seconds, then run a single full re-index (`runPass1`). This is significantly more efficient than processing 100 individual events during a git pull or Obsidian Sync download. Track event count with a rolling window counter, reset when settling completes.
9c. **Add Obsidian Sync conflict file filter:** Add a conflict file filter to `parseJournalFileName()` in `fileNameParser.ts`: reject filenames containing `(Conflict)` (case-insensitive check via `.toLowerCase().includes('(conflict)')`). Obsidian Sync creates conflict files like `2026-03-05, Thursday (Conflict).md` that match the date regex but would create duplicate entries. This is a retroactive fix to Phase 1 indexer code.
10. **Split `types.ts` into `src/types/` modules:** Create `src/types/settings.ts`, `src/types/journal.ts`, `src/types/metrics.ts`, `src/types/insights.ts` (empty for now), and `src/types/index.ts` (barrel re-exports). Move existing interfaces into their respective files. Update all imports across the codebase. See Plan-Wide Rules "Types Organization". **FrontmatterField cleanup:** During this split, resolve the dual `min`/`max` definition ŌĆö remove top-level `min: number` and `max: number` from `FrontmatterField`, keeping only `range?: { min: number; max: number }` (present only for numeric fields). Update all consumers to use `field.range?.min` / `field.range?.max`.
11. **Create `src/utils/periodUtils.ts`:** Shared hub for all period-based aggregation. Initial functions:
    ```typescript
    /** Get entries within the current week/month containing referenceDate */
    export function getEntriesInPeriod(
        entries: JournalEntry[], period: 'week' | 'month',
        referenceDate: Date, weekStartDay?: number
    ): JournalEntry[]

    /** Get start and end dates of the week containing referenceDate */
    export function getWeekBounds(referenceDate: Date, weekStartDay?: number): { start: Date; end: Date }

    /** Get start and end dates of the month containing referenceDate */
    export function getMonthBounds(referenceDate: Date): { start: Date; end: Date }

    /** Aggregate entries by period, extracting a numeric field as data points */
    export function aggregateByPeriod(
        entries: JournalEntry[], fieldKey: string,
        period: 'daily' | 'weekly' | 'monthly', weekStartDay?: number
    ): MetricDataPoint[]
    ```
    `weekStartDay` defaults to auto-detected locale value per Plan-Wide Rules "Week Start Day" (falls back to `0`/Sunday). `MetricsEngine`, `PulseService`, and `ChartDataService` all import from `periodUtils` rather than each implementing their own period iteration logic.
12. **Add `revision` counter to `journalStore`:** Add `revision: number` (starting at 0) to `journalStore` state. Increment it on every `upsertEntry()`, `upsertEntries()`, `removeEntry()`, and `clear()` call. This provides a cheap, reliable change signal that catches edits to existing entries (where `entries.size` stays the same).
13. **Wire `metricsCacheStore` staleness tracking:** In `main.ts onload()`, after store initialization, create a Zustand subscription that watches `journalStore.revision` for entry changes and calls `useMetricsCacheStore.getState().markStale()`. The subscription reads accumulated changed field keys from `journalStore.pendingChangedFieldKeys`, then triggers a debounced `invalidateCache(changedFieldKeys)` after 2 seconds. Store the unsubscribe function in `this.storeSubscriptions` for cleanup in `onunload()`:
    ```typescript
    // In onload(), after journalIndex.initialize():
    const unsubJournal = useJournalStore.subscribe(
        (state) => state.revision,
        () => {
            useMetricsCacheStore.getState().markStale();
            clearTimeout(this.cacheInvalidateTimer);
            this.cacheInvalidateTimer = setTimeout(() => {
                const store = useJournalStore.getState();
                const keys = store.fullInvalidation ? [] : [...store.pendingChangedFieldKeys];
                // Clear accumulated keys after reading
                store.clearPendingChanges();
                useMetricsCacheStore.getState().invalidateCache(keys);
            }, 2000);
        }
    );
    this.storeSubscriptions.push(unsubJournal);
    ```
    **Data flow:** `invalidateCache([])` (empty array) clears all cached data (used on bulk changes like `reconfigure()`). `invalidateCache(['mood', 'sleep'])` clears only the cache entries for those field keys, leaving other fields' caches intact.

    **`pendingChangedFieldKeys` in `journalStore` (replaces `lastChangedEntry`):** Add `pendingChangedFieldKeys: Set<string>` and `fullInvalidation: boolean` to `journalStore` state. `upsertEntry()` adds the upserted entry's frontmatter keys to `pendingChangedFieldKeys`. `upsertEntries()` and `clear()` set `fullInvalidation = true` (batch changes trigger full invalidation). Add `clearPendingChanges()` action that resets `pendingChangedFieldKeys` to empty and `fullInvalidation` to `false`. **Why not `lastChangedEntry`?** With rapid sequential `upsertEntry()` calls, Zustand subscriptions fire asynchronously ŌĆö only the last entry's keys would be seen. The accumulated `Set<string>` approach ensures no keys are lost between rapid updates.
14. **Implement tiered section storage:** Add `sectionHeadings?: string[]`, `firstSectionExcerpt?: string`, and `sectionWordCounts?: Record<string, number>` to `JournalEntry` type. Update `JournalIndexService.runPass2()` to check entry age: entries older than `HOT_TIER_DAYS` store only `sectionHeadings`, `firstSectionExcerpt`, and `sectionWordCounts` instead of full `sections`. **`HOT_TIER_DAYS` is a setting from the start** ŌĆö add `hotTierDays: number` (default `90`) to `HindsightSettings` under Advanced settings. This is a simple number input with a note: "Entries older than this many days store only headings and excerpts instead of full section content. Lower values reduce memory usage. Minimum: 7." Validated in settings tab to be >= 7. **Always populate `firstSectionExcerpt` for ALL entries (hot and cold).** This is ~200 chars ├Ś entries ŌĆö negligible memory (~140KB for 700 entries). Echo cards and timeline cards use `firstSectionExcerpt` directly, eliminating lazy-load I/O for the single most common UI path. Only `SectionReader`, `Lens`, and `Digest` need `ensureSectionsLoaded()` for full section content. Add `ensureSectionsLoaded(filePath): Promise<JournalEntry>` action to `journalStore` for lazy-loading cold entry sections on demand. **`sectionWordCounts`:** Stores per-section word counts (computed during Pass 2, retained for cold tier). This is needed because `getSectionWordCounts()` in Phase 8 (ThreadsService) would otherwise return zero for cold entries, producing misleading section-level word count trends. **Concurrency deduplication (A22 ŌĆö documented contract):** Use a **module-level** in-flight promise map (`Map<string, Promise<JournalEntry>>`) ŌĆö NOT part of Zustand state ŌĆö to coalesce concurrent requests for the same filePath. **Why module-level:** Zustand state must be serializable and immutable-update-friendly; `Map<string, Promise>` is neither. The module-level Map is intentional and documented here as the single source of truth for this design decision. If a load is already in progress, return the existing promise instead of starting a new `vault.cachedRead()` + parse. Clear the map entry on completion (both success and failure) in a `finally` block. Export a `clearInFlightMap()` function for testing (called in `beforeEach` to prevent inter-test state leaks). **Cleanup contract:** `clearInFlightMap()` must also be called from `resetAllStores()` in `storeWiring.ts` during plugin unload to prevent stale promises surviving a disable/re-enable cycle. This prevents duplicate I/O when SectionReader and Lens both request the same cold entry simultaneously. Log estimated sections memory via `debugLog()` after indexing completes. Ensure `ensureSectionsLoaded()` has thorough test coverage in Phase 5.5, since every downstream consumer (SectionReader, Lens, Digest) depends on correct cold-entry lazy-loading.
15. **Add `settingsStore.reset()` action:** Add a `reset()` action to `settingsStore` that returns settings to `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`. Include it in the `onunload()` store reset sequence.
16. **Add `storeSubscriptions` and `cleanupRegistry` arrays to plugin class:** Add `private storeSubscriptions: (() => void)[] = [];` and `private cleanupRegistry: (() => void)[] = [];` to `HindsightPlugin`. Populate `storeSubscriptions` during `onload()` (item 13). Clean up both in `onunload()` ŌĆö subscriptions first, then general cleanup, then store resets (see Plan-Wide Rules "Store Lifecycle").
17. **Add ESLint with guideline-critical rules:** Install `@typescript-eslint/eslint-plugin` and configure these three rules that the Obsidian review bot checks:
    - `@typescript-eslint/no-floating-promises: "error"` ŌĆö #1 most-flagged issue in plugin reviews
    - `no-console: ["error", { allow: ["warn", "error"] }]` ŌĆö bot flags `console.log`. Note: `console.debug` is intentionally NOT in the allow list. All debug output must go through `debugLog()`, which internally calls `console.debug`. This ensures future contributors can't bypass the settings-gated debug output. **ESLint override:** Add a per-file eslint-disable for `src/utils/debugLog.ts` only: `/* eslint-disable no-console */` at the top of that file. The console grep gate (exit gate below) must also exclude `debugLog.ts`: `grep -rn 'console\.debug' src/ --include='*.ts' --include='*.tsx' | grep -v 'debugLog.ts'`.
    - `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any: "error"` ŌĆö bot flags `any` type

   **Priority note:** Complete this IMMEDIATELY after item 0 (promise fix) and item 1 (uPlot removal). Every subsequent new code addition should be validated by lint as it's written, not retroactively after 16 items of new code. Configure `"build": "npm run lint && node esbuild.config.mjs production"` to enforce lint-on-build.
18. **Extract store wiring to `src/storeWiring.ts` (unconditional ŌĆö do not defer):** Create `src/storeWiring.ts` with `wireStoreSubscriptions(plugin: HindsightPluginInterface): (() => void)[]` (all cross-store subscription setup from item 13) and `resetAllStores(): void` (all store reset calls, with `appStore` reset last). `main.ts onload()` becomes `this.storeSubscriptions = wireStoreSubscriptions(this);` and `onunload()` becomes `this.storeSubscriptions.forEach(fn => fn()); this.cleanupRegistry.forEach(fn => fn()); resetAllStores();`. This keeps `main.ts` thin by design (target: ~80-100 lines), not by hope. `main.ts` is already 192 lines pre-cleanup ŌĆö without proactive extraction, the additions from items 7-16 will push it well past 150 even after command extraction.
19. **Create `src/utils/settingsMigration.ts`:** Implement versioned `migrateSettings()` (see Plan-Wide Rules "Settings Schema Migration"). Add `settingsVersion: number` (default `1`) to `HindsightSettings` and `DEFAULT_SETTINGS`. Initial migration: v0 (no version field) ŌåÆ v1 (adds version field + applies defaults). Update `loadSettings()` to call `migrateSettings()`. **Settings validation:** After `migrateSettings()`, run `validateSettings(settings: unknown): HindsightSettings` that checks types and ranges for each field. For each field: validate expected type, valid range (e.g., `thumbnailSize` must be 80/120/160, `hotTierDays` must be >= 7), and fall back to the `DEFAULT_SETTINGS` value if invalid. This catches manual `data.json` edits (e.g., `"thumbnailSize": "banana"`). Especially important for complex nested objects like `goalTargets` and `savedFilters`. Each subsequent phase that adds/renames settings increments the version and adds a migration function. **Downgrade handling:** If `loaded.settingsVersion > CURRENT_MAX_VERSION`, log via `debugLog()` ("Settings version newer than plugin ŌĆö possible downgrade") and skip migration. Do NOT reset settings to defaults on downgrade ŌĆö that would silently lose the user's configuration. **Prototype pollution guard:** Call `sanitizeLoadedData()` on the raw loaded data before applying defaults (see Plan-Wide Rules "Prototype pollution guard").
  **Explicit path validation call sites (amendment):** Phase 5a creates the `validateVaultRelativePath()` validator and wires it to `journalFolder` only. Other path settings (`weeklyReviewFolder`, `exportFolder`) don't exist yet ŌĆö their validation call sites are wired in Phase 10 and Phase 11 respectively, each with their own verification checks. **Defense-in-depth (A9):** `ensureFolderExists()` (in `src/utils/vaultUtils.ts`) must also call `validateVaultRelativePath()` internally, so that any caller ŌĆö even one that forgets to pre-validate ŌĆö is protected against path traversal:
    ```typescript
    export async function ensureFolderExists(vault: Vault, folderPath: string): Promise<void> {
        const validated = validateVaultRelativePath(folderPath);
        if (!validated) throw new Error(`Invalid folder path: ${folderPath}`);
        // ... rest of function using validated path
    }
    ```
 On downgrade, validateSettings still runs normally to catch type mismatches on known keys. It ignores unknown keys added by the newer version.
 **Amendment:** Use range validation (typeof value === number AND value >= 40 AND value <= 320) instead of strict enum checks for numeric settings like thumbnailSize. The settings UI offers preset values, but the validation layer should accept any reasonable number. Apply the same principle to similar numeric settings (e.g., hotTierDays >= 7 AND hotTierDays <= 365).
 **Settings migration contract:** Each migration function is **idempotent** ŌĆö safe to re-run on already-migrated data. On migration failure: log error via `debugLog()`, keep existing settings unchanged, bump `settingsVersion` anyway (prevents infinite retry loops on corrupt data). Run migrations in `loadSettings()` BEFORE any service initialization. Store the raw loaded data in a transient `debugLog()` call for debugging.
20. **Create `src/utils/chartSetup.ts`:** Side-effect module for Chart.js tree-shaking registration. Import and register only the chart types and components actually used (see Plan-Wide Rules "Chart.js Tree-Shaking"). Chart components import this module once ŌĆö registration is idempotent.
21. **Extract `FileWatcherService` from `JournalIndexService`:** `JournalIndexService.ts` is already 396 lines (above the 300-line guideline). Extract all file watcher handlers into `src/services/FileWatcherService.ts` (~150 lines). `FileWatcherService` receives events from Obsidian, debounces them, and calls back into `JournalIndexService` for the actual parsing/indexing work. This splits "what triggers indexing" from "how to index", keeping both files under 300 lines. `JournalIndexService` retains: `initialize()`, `runPass1()`, `runPass2()`, `reconfigure()`, `ensureSectionsLoaded()`, `destroy()`. `FileWatcherService` handles: all `vault.on()` and `metadataCache.on()` registrations, debouncing, bulk settling mode (item 9b), and the schema-dirty flag.
22. **Add `normalizePathSetting()` and `validateVaultRelativePath()` helpers:** Add both to appropriate utility files (see Plan-Wide Rules "Path Safety"). Update the settings tab to validate + normalize `journalFolder` on save. **Note:** This creates the reusable validator and wires it to `journalFolder` only. Other path settings (`exportFolder`, `weeklyReviewFolder`) don't exist yet ŌĆö their call sites are wired in Phase 10 and Phase 11 respectively, each with their own verification checks.
23. **Create `src/utils/sanitize.ts`:** Add the `sanitizeLoadedData()` utility for prototype pollution protection (referenced in item 19 and Plan-Wide Rules). This must strip `__proto__`, `constructor`, and `prototype` keys recursively from any deserialized object:
    ```typescript
    export function sanitizeLoadedData(obj: unknown): unknown {
        if (typeof obj !== 'object' || obj === null) return obj;
        if (Array.isArray(obj)) return obj.map(sanitizeLoadedData);
        const clean: Record<string, unknown> = {};
        for (const key of Object.keys(obj)) {
            if (key === '__proto__' || key === 'constructor' || key === 'prototype') continue;
            clean[key] = sanitizeLoadedData((obj as Record<string, unknown>)[key]);
        }
        return clean;
    }
    ```
    Called from `migrateSettings()` (item 19) on raw loaded data before applying defaults, and from saved filter deserialization in Phase 7.

> **Implementation order:** Session 1: items 1, 2 (EVAL VIEW DELETION FIRST ŌĆö security gate), 0, 3, **6** (create `debugLog` + replace ALL `console.debug`), **17** (ESLint ŌĆö now all existing violations are fixed), 4, 10. The eval views must be the absolute first deletions so the innerHTML grep gate passes immediately. The `console.debug` calls across the ENTIRE codebase must be replaced with `debugLog()` BEFORE ESLint is enabled, otherwise the `no-console` rule fails immediately. Session 2: items 5, 7-9. Session 3: items 11-16, 18-23.

> **Pre-5a async audit (A26):** Before starting item 0, run `grep -rn 'async.*=>' src/ main.ts | grep -E 'addEventListener|setTimeout|on\('` and save the output. Create a checklist proving each async listener site is wrapped (`void`, `await`, or `.catch`). This artifact must exist before proceeding.

**Phase 5a is effectively 3 sub-sessions** due to its 23 items. Suggested session boundaries: Session 1: items 0-4, 6, 10, 17 (cleanup + debugLog + ESLint + infrastructure). Session 2: items 5, 7-9 (stores + indexing + debouncing). Session 3: items 11-16, 18-22 (remaining utilities, migration, wiring).

## Phase 5b: Chart Engine + Tab Groups + Sparklines (~1-2 sessions)

**Goal:** Install Chart.js, build the chart data pipeline, create reusable chart and sparkline components, and restructure the main view with tab groups. This phase establishes all charting infrastructure ŌĆö later phases just compose it.

**Before Phase 5b:** MainApp has a flat tab bar -- Calendar | Timeline | Index.

**After Phase 5b:** MainApp uses a two-tier navigation:
- **Top bar:** Tab group switcher -- Journal | Insights | Explore
- **Secondary bar:** Sub-tabs within the active group

| Group | Sub-tabs | Purpose |
|-------|----------|---------|
| **Journal** | Calendar, Timeline, Index | Core navigation -- "show me my entries" |
| **Insights** | Charts, Pulse, Digest | Analytics -- "show me patterns" |
| **Explore** | Lens, Threads, Gallery | Discovery -- "let me dig into specifics" |

Pulse, Digest, Lens, Threads, and Gallery render `EmptyState` stubs until their respective phases.

### Files to Create

**`src/components/shared/TabGroup.tsx`** (~50 lines)

Two-tier tab navigation component:
- Props: `groups: { id: string; label: string; tabs: { id: string; label: string }[] }[]`, `activeGroup: string`, `activeTab: string`, `onGroupChange: (id: string) => void`, `onTabChange: (id: string) => void`
- Top bar renders group buttons with `hindsight-tab-group` class (larger, bolder than sub-tabs)
- Secondary bar renders sub-tab buttons for the active group with `hindsight-tab-sub` class
- Both bars use 44px touch targets
- CSS classes: `hindsight-tab-group-bar`, `hindsight-tab-sub-bar`, `hindsight-tab-group`, `hindsight-tab-group-active`, `hindsight-tab-sub`, `hindsight-tab-sub-active`

**`src/services/ChartDataService.ts`** (~150 lines)

Transforms journal data into Chart.js-ready datasets:
```typescript
import type { JournalEntry, FrontmatterField, MetricDataPoint, DateRange } from '../types';

/**
 * Extract a time series for a specific frontmatter field.
 * Returns sorted MetricDataPoint[] with null for missing values.
 * Reuses FrontmatterService.getFieldTimeSeries() internally.
 */
export function getTimeSeries(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fieldKey: string,
    range?: DateRange
): MetricDataPoint[]

/**
 * Compute a rolling average over a time series.
 * windowSize: number of data points in the rolling window (default 7).
 * Null values are skipped in the average calculation.
 */
export function rollingAverage(
    data: MetricDataPoint[],
    windowSize?: number
): MetricDataPoint[]

/**
 * Compute a simple linear trend line (least squares regression).
 * Returns slope, intercept, and two endpoint data points for Chart.js line overlay.
 * Skips null values in the regression.
 */
export function trendLine(
    data: MetricDataPoint[]
): { slope: number; intercept: number; points: MetricDataPoint[] }

/**
 * Build a Chart.js-compatible dataset config for a single metric.
 * Includes labels (dates), data values, colors from CSS variables.
 */
export function buildChartDataset(
    data: MetricDataPoint[],
    label: string,
    color: string
): { labels: string[]; datasets: object[] }

/**
 * Build a multi-metric overlay dataset (e.g., mood + energy on same chart).
 * Each metric gets its own Y axis if scales differ significantly.
 */
export function buildMultiMetricDataset(
    series: { data: MetricDataPoint[]; label: string; color: string }[]
): { labels: string[]; datasets: object[] }
```

**`src/store/chartUiStore.ts`** (~30 lines)

UI state for the Charts/Insights tabs. Separated from cache to avoid mixing concerns (see Plan-Wide Rules "Store Lifecycle").

**Persistence model:** `selectedChartFields` and `rollingWindow` are **mirrored from settings** ŌĆö they are loaded from `HindsightSettings` on plugin start and written back via `saveSettingsDebounced()` on change. This ensures they survive reload (they represent deliberate user preferences, not transient navigation). `dismissedAlertIds` and `chartDateRange` are session-only (transient, reset on reload).
```typescript
import { create } from 'zustand';

interface ChartUiState {
    /** Selected fields for the Charts tab */
    selectedChartFields: string[];
    /** Date range for chart display */
    chartDateRange: { start: Date; end: Date } | null;
    /** Rolling average window size (days) */
    rollingWindow: number;
    /** Dismissed trend alert IDs for the current session. Plain array, not Set, to ensure
     *  immutable updates trigger re-renders. Reset on plugin reload. */
    dismissedAlertIds: string[];
 **Cap:** ``dismissedAlertIds`` is capped at 500 entries (FIFO). When the array exceeds 500, the oldest entries are dropped. This prevents unbounded growth during long sessions with frequent trend alert regeneration. The array resets on session reload regardless, so the cap is insurance against runaway sessions. At ~50 bytes per ID, 500 entries = ~25KB, which is negligible.
}

interface ChartUiActions {
    setSelectedChartFields(fields: string[]): void;
    setChartDateRange(range: { start: Date; end: Date } | null): void;
    setRollingWindow(window: number): void;
    /** Add an alert ID to the dismissed list. Uses immutable update (new array). */
    dismissAlert(id: string): void;
    /** Reset to initial state (called from plugin.onunload()) */
    reset(): void;
}
```

**`src/store/metricsCacheStore.ts`** (~50 lines)

Computed data cache with staleness tracking. Separate from UI state:
```typescript
import { create } from 'zustand';
import type { MetricDataPoint } from '../types';

interface MetricsCacheState {
    /** Cached time series per field key. Invalidated when entries change. */
    timeSeriesCache: Map<string, MetricDataPoint[]>;
    /** Cached rolling averages per field key + window size. */
    rollingAverageCache: Map<string, MetricDataPoint[]>;
    /** Cache key: entry count + latest mtime. Only invalidate fields that changed. */
    cacheKey: { entryCount: number; latestMtime: number };
    /** Cached correlation results (computed once per entry change, not per render) */
    correlationResults: { field1: string; field2: string; r: number }[] | null;
  **Granular correlation invalidation (amendment):** Instead of always clearing all correlationResults, check whether any changedFieldKeys appear in the cached correlation pairs. Only invalidate if a changed field participates in a cached correlation. cachedAlerts are still always cleared (alerts may reference any field).
    /** Cached trend alerts (computed once per entry change, not per render) */
    cachedAlerts: TrendAlert[] | null;
    /** Cached weekly comparison (this week vs last week, computed once per entry change) */
    cachedWeeklyComparison: { field: string; thisWeek: number; lastWeek: number; change: number; percentChange: number }[] | null;
    /** Whether cached data is stale (entry changed but recomputation pending) */
    stale: boolean;
}

interface MetricsCacheActions {
    /**
     * Mark cache as stale immediately when entries change.
     * Components show a subtle "Updating..." indicator while stale.
     */
    markStale(): void;
    /**
     * Granular invalidation: clears cached data only for the specified fields.
     * Called with changedFieldKeys after 2s debounce. Empty array = full clear
     * (used on bulk changes like reconfigure/clear).
     * Sets stale = false when complete.
     */
    invalidateCache(changedFieldKeys: string[]): void;
    /**
     * Get time series for a field. This is a PURE CACHE ŌĆö it stores and retrieves data only.
     * It does NOT read from journalStore internally. Instead, the `useChartData()` hook
     * reads entries from journalStore and passes them to ChartDataService on cache miss,
     * then stores the result here. Cache key includes journalStore.revision for staleness.
     */
    getTimeSeries(fieldKey: string): MetricDataPoint[] | null;
    setTimeSeries(fieldKey: string, data: MetricDataPoint[]): void;
    /** Reset to initial state (called from plugin.onunload()) */
    reset(): void;
}
```

**Cache staleness pattern:** When journal entries change, `markStale()` is called immediately (sets `stale = true`). Components reading from the cache check `stale` and show a subtle "Updating..." indicator **wrapped in `aria-live="polite"`** for screen reader accessibility. The actual `invalidateCache(changedFieldKeys)` runs after a 2-second debounce. If `changedFieldKeys` is non-empty, only those fields' entries are cleared from `timeSeriesCache` and `rollingAverageCache`; `correlationResults` are only cleared if a changed field participates in a cached correlation pair (granular check). `cachedAlerts` are only cleared if a changed field appears in a cached alert's `relatedFields` list. **`cachedWeeklyComparison` is always cleared on any invalidation** (it iterates all numeric fields and is cheap to recompute ŌĆö granular invalidation is not worth the complexity). If `changedFieldKeys` is empty, all caches are cleared (full invalidation). This gives the user visual feedback that data is refreshing without hammering the CPU on every keystroke.
**Data flow:** `Component ŌåÆ useChartData() hook ŌåÆ reads metricsCacheStore.getTimeSeries(fieldKey)` ŌåÆ on cache miss (`null`), hook **triggers computation in a `useEffect`** (not inline during render ŌĆö writing to a Zustand store during render violates React's render purity contract and can cause infinite render loops). The effect reads entries from `journalStore.getState()`, calls `ChartDataService.getTimeSeries(entries, fieldKey)`, and stores the result via `metricsCacheStore.getState().setTimeSeries()`. The component renders with the cached value (possibly empty `[]` on first render), then re-renders when the effect completes and the store updates. `ChartDataService` remains a pure stateless calculator; `metricsCacheStore` is a pure cache (stores/retrieves only, never reaches into other stores). This separation makes `metricsCacheStore` testable without mocking `journalStore`.

**`src/hooks/useMetrics.ts`** (~20 lines)
```typescript
/** Subscribe to chartUiStore + metricsCacheStore for chart config and data */
export function useMetrics()

/** Get chart-ready time series for a field, with caching.
 *  Uses useEffect for cache-miss computation (NOT inline during render).
 *  Returns cached value (possibly empty [] on first render); re-renders
 *  when the effect completes and the store updates. */
export function useChartData(fieldKey: string): {
    data: MetricDataPoint[];
    rolling: MetricDataPoint[];
    trend: { slope: number; intercept: number };
}
```

**`src/components/charts/MetricChart.tsx`** (~100 lines)

Chart.js wrapper component:
- Props: `fields: string[]`, `dateRange?: DateRange`, `showRolling?: boolean`, `showTrend?: boolean`, `height?: number`
- Creates a `<canvas>` ref, initializes Chart.js `Line` chart in `useEffect`
- **Canvas null guard:** `useEffect` must check `if (!canvasRef.current) return;` before creating the Chart instance. This prevents crashes in StrictMode or slow renders where the canvas isn't mounted yet.
- **Theme-aware:** reads Obsidian CSS variables (`--text-normal`, `--background-primary`, `--interactive-accent`, `--text-muted`) via `getComputedStyle()` and feeds them into Chart.js config
- **Theme-reactive:** follows the exact Chart.js cleanup pattern from Plan-Wide Rules ŌĆö subscribes to `css-change`, cleans up with `off()` + `chart.destroy()` in the `useEffect` return. **Theme update debounce:** Chart.js `update()` re-renders the entire canvas, which is expensive. Debounce the `css-change` handler by 200ms to avoid excessive canvas redraws during rapid theme switching (e.g., testing CSS snippets).
- Uses `const app = useAppStore(s => s.app); if (!app) return null;` (not `app!` ŌĆö see Plan-Wide Rules) to access `workspace.on/off`
- Reads entries from `journalStore` internally via `useChartData()` hook (no entries prop needed)
- Supports multi-metric overlay (dual Y axes when ranges differ by >10x)
- Click handler on data points: shows a small popover with that day's excerpt (uses `stripMarkdown()` on first non-empty section, truncated to 200 chars)
- Responsive: `maintainAspectRatio: false`, container controls height
- **MUST disable default Chart.js tooltip plugin:** Set `plugins: { tooltip: { enabled: false } }` in the chart config. The default Chart.js tooltip plugin uses `innerHTML` internally, which is a [BLOCKER] per Obsidian guidelines. Use the React-rendered `<div>` tooltip layer instead (same pattern as the Heatmap tooltip).
- **Canvas accessibility:** The `<canvas>` element must have `role="img"` and a descriptive `aria-label` dynamically generated from selected fields and date range (e.g., `aria-label="Line chart showing mood and energy over the last 30 days"`).
- **Error handling (A20):** Wrap Chart.js initialization and `chart.update()` calls inside `useEffect` with `try/catch`. Chart.js can throw on canvas context loss, `Infinity`/`NaN` data, or corrupt datasets. On error, set a local error state and render an inline message: "Chart rendering failed. Try selecting different fields." Log via `console.error`.
- CSS class: `hindsight-chart-container`

**`src/components/charts/Sparkline.tsx`** (~60 lines)
 Add role="img" and aria-label="Sparkline showing {fieldName} trend" to the svg element.

React SVG inline mini-chart:

    journal: 'calendar' | 'timeline' | 'index';

## Phase 5c: Correlation Discovery + Trend Alerts + Field Polarity (~1-2 sessions) Ō£ģ COMPLETED 2026-03-09

**Goal:** Build the MetricsEngine for cross-field analysis, the TrendAlertEngine for proactive user-agnostic insights, field polarity settings, and polarity-aware color-coded badges across all components.

### Settings Updates

Add to `HindsightSettings`:
```typescript
/** Per-field polarity setting: determines badge coloring and trend alert tone */
fieldPolarity: Record<string, 'higher-is-better' | 'lower-is-better' | 'neutral'>;
```
Default: `{}` (all fields default to `'neutral'` when not configured).

Settings tab: new "Field configuration" section listing all detected numeric fields. Each field gets a dropdown: "Higher is better" (green for high values), "Lower is better" (green for low values), "Neutral" (no directional coloring). This section auto-populates from `detectedFields`.

### Files to Create

**`src/services/MetricsEngine.ts`** (~200 lines)

Statistical analysis engine -- all pure functions, no Obsidian API dependency:
```typescript
import type { JournalEntry, MetricDataPoint, FrontmatterField } from '../types';

/**
 * Compute Pearson correlation coefficient between two numeric field series.
 * Returns r value (-1 to 1). Only uses data points where both fields have values.
 * Returns null if fewer than 5 paired data points (insufficient for meaningful correlation).
 */
export function pearsonCorrelation(
    seriesA: MetricDataPoint[],
    seriesB: MetricDataPoint[]
): number | null

/**
 * Compute conditional average: average of fieldA when booleanField is true vs false.
 * Returns { whenTrue, whenFalse, difference, sampleSizeTrue, sampleSizeFalse }.
 * Returns null if either group has fewer than 3 data points.
 */
export function conditionalAverage(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    numericField: string,
    booleanField: string
): { whenTrue: number; whenFalse: number; difference: number; sampleSizeTrue: number; sampleSizeFalse: number } | null

/**
 * Find all significant correlations across all numeric field pairs.
 * Significance threshold: |r| >= 0.4 (moderate or stronger correlation).
 * Returns sorted by absolute r value (strongest first).
 *
 * PERFORMANCE: Capped at 20 numeric fields on desktop, **10 on mobile**
 **Zero-variance guard:** Pre-filter fields in ``findCorrelations()``: exclude any field with variance < 0.0001 (e.g., user always logs the same value for mood). This prevents NaN results from division-by-zero in the Pearson formula and avoids wasted CPU cycles on fields that cannot have meaningful correlations.
 * (`Platform.isMobile ? 10 : 20`). Desktop: C(20,2) = 190 pairs max.
 * Mobile: C(10,2) = 45 pairs max (keeps mobile computation under 200ms).
 * If more fields detected, uses the top N by stable ranking:
 * 1st: numeric fields over boolean (more correlation signal),
 * 2nd: coverage descending (fields appearing in more entries have more data),
 * 3rd: fields the user has previously charted (from selectedChartFields setting),
 * 4th: variance descending,
 * 5th: fieldKey ascending (alphabetical tie-break).
 * This ensures the most useful correlations are computed first.
 * Show in the UI: "Analyzing top N of {total} fields by data coverage" when capped.
 **Analyze all fields toggle (amendment):** When fields are capped, show an "Analyze all fields" toggle (hidden by default, shown only when capping is active). When toggled on, use the full field set. Show the computing-all-fields warning **every time** an uncapped computation starts on mobile (not just on toggle) ŌĆö if `Platform.isMobile && analyzeAll && fields.length > 10`, show "Analyzing all fields..." status indicator on CorrelationCards. The toggle is session-only (transient in ``chartUiStore``, not persisted in settings).
 * Results are cached in metricsCacheStore.correlationResults and only
 * recomputed when entries change (not on every render/tab switch).
 *
 * **SIMPLIFICATION:** With the 20-field cap, correlations complete in <50ms.
 * Use a plain `for` loop with a signal check instead of `processWithYielding()`:
 * ```typescript
 * for (const [a, b] of pairs) {
 *     if (signal?.cancelled) return [];
 *     // compute correlation
 * }
 * ```
 * Reserve `processWithYielding` for genuinely long-running operations.
 * The primary value of the signal here is cancellation on tab switch, not yielding.
 *
 * CRITICAL: Pre-compute all time series arrays ONCE before entering the
 * pair loop. Then pearsonCorrelation() iterates pre-computed arrays instead
 * of re-extracting the same field values from entries multiple times:
 *   const seriesMap = new Map<string, MetricDataPoint[]>();
 *   for (const field of topFields) {
 *       seriesMap.set(field.key, getFieldTimeSeries(entries, field.key));
 *   }
 * This avoids redundant field extractions.
 */
export async function findCorrelations(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fields: FrontmatterField[],
    signal?: { cancelled: boolean }
): Promise<{ fieldA: string; fieldB: string; r: number; n: number }[]>

/**
 * Find all significant conditional averages across all numeric+boolean pairs.
 * Significance threshold: |difference| >= 0.5 AND sampleSize >= 5 per group.
 *
 * PERFORMANCE: Capped at top 10 boolean fields by coverage, paired with
 * top 20 numeric fields (from findCorrelations' stable ranking) = 200 pairs max.
 * If more fields detected, show: "Analyzing top 10 boolean ├Ś 20 numeric fields."
 */
export function findConditionalInsights(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fields: FrontmatterField[]
): { numericField: string; booleanField: string; whenTrue: number; whenFalse: number; difference: number }[]

/**
 * Compute weekly comparison: this week's averages vs last week's for all numeric fields.
 * Returns fields with notable changes (>= 15% or >= 1 unit difference).
 * Results are cached in metricsCacheStore.cachedWeeklyComparison and invalidated
 * when entries change, since this iterates all entries twice (this week + last week).
 */
export function weeklyComparison(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fields: FrontmatterField[],
    referenceDate: Date,
    weekStartDay?: number  // defaults to 0 (Sunday); uses getWeekBounds() from periodUtils
): { field: string; thisWeek: number; lastWeek: number; change: number; percentChange: number }[]
```

**`src/services/TrendAlertEngine.ts`** (~180 lines)

User-agnostic heuristic alert engine -- pure functions operating on field types and statistical patterns, not semantic meaning. No hardcoded field names. Works for any vault's frontmatter:
```typescript
import type { JournalEntry, FrontmatterField } from '../types';

/** Alert severity levels */
export type AlertSeverity = 'info' | 'warning' | 'positive';

/** A generated trend alert */
export interface TrendAlert {
    /** Stable ID for session-level dismissal tracking.
     *  Format: `${alertType}-${fieldKey}-${triggerDate_ISO}`
     *  e.g. 'consecutive-decrease-mood-2026-03-07'
     *  This ensures: dismissing stays dismissed for the session;
     *  if data changes, a new alert with a different date gets a new ID. */
    id: string;
    severity: AlertSeverity;
    title: string;
    body: string;
    /** The field(s) this alert relates to */
    relatedFields: string[];
    /** Entry date that triggered the alert, if applicable */
    triggerDate?: Date;
    /** Entry to link to for context, if applicable */
    relatedEntryPath?: string;
}

/**
 * Detect consecutive directional changes in a numeric field.
 * Generates alerts like: "Field X has decreased 3 days in a row."
 * If polarity is set, adjusts severity: a decrease in a "higher-is-better"
 * field is a warning; in a "lower-is-better" field it's positive.
 * Threshold: 3+ consecutive days in the same direction.
 */
export function detectConsecutiveChange(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fieldKey: string,
    polarity: 'higher-is-better' | 'lower-is-better' | 'neutral'
): TrendAlert | null

/**
 * Detect anomalies: today's value is >= 2 standard deviations from 30-day average.
 * Generates alerts like: "Today's X (2) is unusually low -- your 30-day average is 6.8."
 */
export function detectAnomaly(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fieldKey: string,
    referenceDate: Date
): TrendAlert | null

/**
 * Detect gaps in data collection.
 * Generates alerts like: "You haven't logged X in 5 days."
 * Only alerts for fields with >= 50% historical coverage
 * (avoids nagging about rarely-used fields).
 */
export function detectFieldGap(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fieldKey: string,
    coverage: number,
    referenceDate: Date
): TrendAlert | null

/**
 * Pattern recall: find the last time a similar pattern occurred and what happened next.
 * E.g., "Last time X dropped below Y for 3+ days was [date].
 *        Over the next 5 days, it recovered to Z."
 * Purely statistical -- looks for consecutive-decrease matching current streak length,
 * then reports the recovery trajectory (average of next 5 values after the pattern ended).
 */
export function patternRecall(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fieldKey: string,
    currentStreakLength: number,
    referenceDate: Date
): TrendAlert | null

/**
 * Generate all applicable alerts for the current state.
 * Iterates all numeric and boolean fields, runs each heuristic, deduplicates,
 * and returns sorted by severity (warnings first, then info, then positive).
 * Caps at MAX_ALERTS (default 5) to avoid overwhelming the user.
 */
export function generateAlerts(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fields: FrontmatterField[],
    polarity: Record<string, 'higher-is-better' | 'lower-is-better' | 'neutral'>,
    referenceDate: Date
): TrendAlert[]
```

**`src/utils/statsUtils.ts`** -- Add polarity-aware color function:
```typescript
/**
 * Get badge color for a field value based on polarity setting.
 * - 'higher-is-better': high=green, low=red (default HSL gradient)
 * - 'lower-is-better': high=red, low=green (inverted gradient)
 * - 'neutral': consistent blue (no directional meaning)
 */
export function getPolarityColor(
    value: number | null,
    min: number,
    max: number,
    polarity: 'higher-is-better' | 'lower-is-better' | 'neutral'
): string
```

**`src/components/charts/ScatterPlot.tsx`** (~90 lines)

Interactive scatter plot using Chart.js `Scatter` type:
- Props: `fields: FrontmatterField[]`
- Reads entries from `journalStore` internally
- **Theme-reactive:** subscribes to `app.workspace.on('css-change')` (same pattern as MetricChart)
- Two dropdowns: X-axis field, Y-axis field (filtered to numeric fields)
- Optional third dropdown: color-by field (boolean fields only -- dots colored by true/false)
- Each dot = one journal entry day
- Hover tooltip: date + both values
- Click handler: opens the note for that entry
 **File-exists guard:** Before opening, check ``app.vault.getFileByPath(entry.filePath)``. If ``null``, show a Notice: "Entry file no longer exists." Apply the same guard to Heatmap click handlers and Gallery click handlers.
- Shows Pearson r value in the corner (via `MetricsEngine.pearsonCorrelation()`)
- Regression line overlay
- **MUST disable default Chart.js tooltip plugin:** Set `plugins: { tooltip: { enabled: false } }` in the chart config (same as MetricChart ŌĆö the default tooltip uses `innerHTML` which is a [BLOCKER]).
- **Canvas accessibility:** The `<canvas>` element must have `role="img"` and a descriptive `aria-label` (e.g., `aria-label="Scatter plot showing mood vs sleep duration"`).
- CSS class: `hindsight-scatter-plot`

**`src/components/charts/CorrelationCards.tsx`** (~70 lines)

Auto-generated insight cards:
- **Reads from `metricsCacheStore.correlationResults`** (cached, not computed on mount)
- If cache is null, triggers async computation which stores results in metricsCacheStore. **Debounced trigger (500ms):** to prevent wasted computation when the user rapidly switches tabs (Journal ŌåÆ Insights ŌåÆ Journal ŌåÆ Insights), the cache-miss computation is delayed by 500ms. If the user switches away within 500ms, the computation never starts. Combined with the existing `signal` cancellation on tab-switch-away, this provides two layers of protection against unnecessary work.
- Renders a card per significant finding:
  - Correlation: "mood and sleep_duration are correlated (r = 0.65, based on 180 entries)"
  - Conditional: "Your average mood on workout days is 7.2 vs 5.8 on non-workout days"
- Sorted by significance, limited to top 10
- Each card clickable -- opens ScatterPlot with those fields pre-selected
- CSS class: `hindsight-correlation-card`

**`src/components/insights/TrendAlertCard.tsx`** (~40 lines)

Renders a single TrendAlert:
- Props: `alert: TrendAlert`
- Color-coded left border: `info` = blue, `warning` = amber, `positive` = green
- Shows title (bold), body text, optional "View entry" link
- CSS class: `hindsight-trend-alert`

**`src/components/insights/TrendAlertsPanel.tsx`** (~40 lines)

Container for trend alerts (Charts tab and optionally sidebar):
- **Reads from `metricsCacheStore.cachedAlerts`** (computed once per entry change, not per render)
- If cache is null, triggers async `generateAlerts()` which stores results in metricsCacheStore
- If `metricsCacheStore.stale` is true, shows a subtle "Updating..." indicator
- Renders list of `TrendAlertCard` components
- "Dismiss" button per card (dismissed IDs stored in `uiStore` for the session)
- Empty state: "No notable trends right now. Keep journaling!"
- CSS class: `hindsight-trend-alerts`

## Phase 6a: Pulse Dashboard + Heatmap + Personal Bests (~1-2 sessions) Use fixed trend window sizes: `[7, 14, 30]` days. Use `processWithYielding()` for the outer field loop. If >10 numeric fields detected, limit to top 5 by data coverage to keep mobile computation under 200ms.

**STATUS: Ō£ģ COMPLETED (2026-03-09)**

**Goal:** Build the core Pulse analytics dashboard with a GitHub-style heatmap, habit streak tracking, personal bests, and consistency scoring. This is the "at a glance, how am I doing?" view.

### Files to Create

**`src/components/charts/Heatmap.tsx`** (~120 lines)

GitHub-style contribution/mood heatmap (React SVG, no external library):
- Props: `fieldKey: string`, `polarity: string`, `months?: number` (default 12)
- Reads entries from `journalStore` internally
- Renders a grid of small squares: columns = weeks, rows = days of week (Mon-Sun)
- Color intensity based on field value, using `getPolarityColor()` for polarity-awareness
- Empty days = `--background-modifier-border` (barely visible)
- Hover tooltip: date and field value only (no tags ŌĆö tags can be long and numerous, cluttering the tooltip). Tooltip is a **React-rendered `<div>`** positioned via state (not a CSS pseudo-element with `attr()`), keeping all content in JSX auto-escape land.
- **Accessibility:** Do NOT annotate each individual `<rect>` with `aria-label` attributes ŌĆö 365 rects ├Ś 3 attributes creates significant DOM overhead on mobile. Instead, provide a **visually-hidden `<table>` alternative** for screen readers: render a `<table>` with `class="sr-only"` (visually hidden but screen-reader-accessible) that contains the same data as the heatmap grid. The `<svg>` heatmap has `aria-hidden="true"` (the table provides the accessible version). The `<table>` uses standard `<th>` for day-of-week headers and `<td>` for values. The `.sr-only` class uses the standard clip-rect technique (`position: absolute; width: 1px; height: 1px; overflow: hidden; clip: rect(0, 0, 0, 0);`). The SVG root still has `role="img"` with a descriptive `aria-label` for context (e.g., `aria-label="Heatmap showing mood over the last 12 months"`).
- **Event delegation:** single `onClick` handler on the SVG container, identifies cell via `event.target.dataset.date`. Same for hover. No per-rect event listeners.
- **Heatmap displays 1 year at a time** (year navigation buttons, not multi-year render). This caps SVG elements at ~365 `<rect>` nodes.
- **Cell performance:** Cell components wrapped in `React.memo()` ŌĆö only re-render on value/color change. Drag selection uses event delegation on the SVG container, NOT per-cell handlers. `pointermove` throttled via `requestAnimationFrame` during drag.
- **CSS:** `.hindsight-heatmap svg { touch-action: none; }` on desktop to prevent scroll interference during drag-select. On mobile, drag-select is disabled entirely so this has no effect.
- Click a square -> opens that day's note via `app.workspace.openLinkText()`
- Click-and-drag to select a date range ŌåÆ updates `uiStore.chartDateRange` (filters Charts tab). **Drag UX (imperative DOM ŌĆö keeps React out of the hot loop):** During drag, use refs (not React state) for the provisional range and apply CSS classes directly on SVG elements for visual feedback:
  - On `pointerdown`: store start cell index in a ref
  - On `pointermove`: use a pre-built `Map<string, SVGRectElement>` populated via a `useEffect` + `querySelectorAll('[data-date]')` stored in a `useRef`. **Lifecycle:** Clear and rebuild the map when the field or month range changes (add these to the effect's dependency array) ŌĆö old map entries would reference stale DOM nodes after re-renders. On `pointermove`, iterate only the date range from the map ŌĆö O(R) where R is the selection range, not O(N) via `querySelectorAll` over all 365 cells ŌĆö and apply `classList.add/remove` on the SVG `<rect>` elements for visual feedback. No `setState` calls during drag.
 **Amendment:** Instead of querySelectorAll in a useEffect, use a ref callback pattern on each rect element to register/unregister from the Map as elements mount/unmount. This avoids the timing issue where useEffect runs before new month cells are in the DOM. Alternatively, use useLayoutEffect (synchronous after DOM mutations) with a guard: if the queried element count does not match the expected cell count for the current month, skip the map rebuild.
  - On `pointerup`: read start/end from refs, commit to `uiStore.chartDateRange`, and remove CSS classes.
  - **Cleanup:** Add `pointercancel` and unmount cleanup (via `useEffect` return) that reset drag state and remove CSS classes without committing a date range. This prevents phantom date-range commits when the user navigates away mid-drag.
- **Mobile:** Disable drag-select on mobile (`Platform.isMobile`). Instead, provide two date picker inputs ("From" / "To") below the heatmap for custom range selection. Tapping a single cell opens that day's note (unchanged). Date presets (30d, 90d, 1yr) remain available in the Charts tab. Additionally, render the date range picker inputs **above** the heatmap (before it in the DOM) on mobile, not below ŌĆö users shouldn't have to scroll past a 12-month chart to reach date selection controls.
- **Mobile tooltips (tap-to-show):** On mobile, hover tooltips don't exist. Instead, tapping a heatmap cell shows its tooltip persistently until the user taps another cell or taps outside the heatmap. Implementation: on tap, set `focusedCell` state to the tapped cell's date; render tooltip for `focusedCell`. A second tap on a different cell updates `focusedCell`. Tapping outside the SVG container (via a `document` click listener) clears `focusedCell`. This is more discoverable than long-press for a grid of small cells.
- **Keyboard navigation:** Make the heatmap container `tabIndex={0}` and focusable. When focused:
  - Arrow Left/Right: navigate to previous/next day
  - Arrow Up/Down: navigate to previous/next week-row (same day-of-week)
  - Enter: open the focused cell's note
  - Track focused cell via a `focusedDate` ref. Update `aria-activedescendant` on the SVG to point to the focused `<rect>` element's ID for screen reader tracking.
  - Visual focus indicator: add a `hindsight-heatmap-cell-focused` CSS class to the focused cell (2px solid outline using `--interactive-accent`).

- CSS class: `hindsight-heatmap`

**`src/components/charts/HabitStreaksGrid.tsx`** (~80 lines)

Boolean field streak visualization:
- Props: `booleanFields: FrontmatterField[]`
- Reads entries from `journalStore` internally
- One row per boolean field (morning_meds_taken, workout, light_therapy, etc.)
- Each row: field label, last 90 days as small colored squares (green=true, gray=false/missing), current streak count
- **Performance:** `getHabitStreaks()` result is memoized with `useMemo` keyed on `journalStore.revision` (not `entries.length`, which misses in-place value edits) and a stable field-key hash. Only recomputes when entries actually change.
- Compact display -- de-emphasized, informational not gamified
- **Accessibility:** Each habit square has `aria-label` with date and status (e.g., `aria-label="March 7: completed"` or `aria-label="March 7: not completed"`). The `<svg>` root has `role="img"` with a descriptive `aria-label`.
- CSS class: `hindsight-habit-grid`

**`src/components/pulse/PulsePanel.tsx`** (~60 lines)

Layout container for the Pulse sub-tab:
- Renders sections in order: StatsCards, Heatmap, PersonalBests, ConsistencyScore, HabitStreaksGrid
- Each section collapsible with a header
- CSS class: `hindsight-pulse-panel`

**`src/components/pulse/StatsCards.tsx`** (~50 lines)

Summary stat cards row:
- Props: `entries: JournalEntry[]`, `fields: FrontmatterField[]`
- Cards: Total entries, Current streak, Average mood (or first numeric field), This week's entry count
- Each card: large number, label below, subtle background
- CSS class: `hindsight-stats-cards`

**`src/components/pulse/PersonalBests.tsx`** (~70 lines)

Achievement-style cards (informational, not gamified):
- Props: `fields: FrontmatterField[]`
- Reads entries from `journalStore` internally
- **Performance:** Personal bests are cached in `metricsCacheStore` via a dedicated `cachedPersonalBests: PersonalBest[] | null` field. Invalidated when `stale` is set to `true`. **Use a 2-second debounce for recomputation** (matching the `metricsCacheStore` invalidation debounce ŌĆö personal bests computation is fast, so a shorter debounce is acceptable and reduces the stale-data window after edits). Invalidation is tracked via a simple `personalBestsStale: boolean` flag; the debounced recompute runs only when this flag is `true`.
- Computes and displays:
  - "Highest [field] week: March 3-9, 2025 (avg 8.1)" -- best 7-day rolling average for each numeric field
  - "Most consistent month: January 2026 (30/31 days journaled)" -- month with highest entry count / days ratio
  - "Best [field] trend: 8 -> 3 over October 2025" -- largest positive trend (respects polarity for "positive" direction)
- Limit to top 5 personal bests to avoid overwhelming
- CSS class: `hindsight-personal-bests`

**`src/components/pulse/ConsistencyScore.tsx`** (~40 lines)

Weekly/monthly consistency display:
- Props: `entries: JournalEntry[]`, `referenceDate: Date`
- Shows: "This week: 5/7 (71%)", "This month: 22/28 (79%)", "All time: 347/730 (48%)"
- Simple bar or percentage display, not a complex chart
- CSS class: `hindsight-consistency`

## Phase 6b: Goals + Today Tab Enhancements (~1-2 sessions) [COMPLETED]

**Goal:** Goal tracking with progress rings, morning briefing panel, and gap alerts -- all integrated into the sidebar Today tab as scrollable sections.

### Settings Updates

Add to `HindsightSettings`:
```typescript
/** Goal targets: field key -> { period, target, type } */
goalTargets: Record<string, {
    period: 'weekly' | 'monthly';
    target: number;
    /** 'sum' for cumulative (studying_hours), 'count' for occurrences (workout) */
    type: 'sum' | 'count';
}>;
/** Whether to show the morning briefing section in sidebar */
morningBriefingEnabled: boolean;
/** Section heading to extract priorities from yesterday's entry */
prioritySectionHeading: string;  // default: "Tomorrow's Top 3"
/** Day the week starts on: 0 = Sunday, 1 = Monday */
weekStartDay: 0 | 1;
```
Default: `weekStartDay` defaults to auto-detected locale value via `new Intl.Locale(navigator.language).weekInfo?.firstDay ?? 0` (falls back to Sunday if locale detection fails). See Plan-Wide Rules "Week Start Day".

Settings tab additions:
- "Goals" section: list of configured goals with add/edit/remove. Each goal: field dropdown (numeric + boolean), period dropdown, target number input, type dropdown.
- **Goal target validation:** `target` must be a positive number (`> 0`). Settings UI: number input with `min="0.1"`. Defense-in-depth in `getGoalProgress()`: if `target <= 0`, return `{ current: 0, target: 1, progress: 0 }` to prevent division by zero in progress rings.
- "Week start day" dropdown: Sunday / Monday. Controls all weekly aggregations (goal progress, weekly review, consistency scores, Digest "this week"). Note: echo week matching (`getISOWeek()`) is unaffected ŌĆö it always uses ISO weeks (Monday start) for cross-year consistency.
- "Morning Briefing" toggle (already exists as `morningBriefingEnabled`)

## Phase 6i: Numeric-Text Field Type (Interjected) Ō£ģ COMPLETED 2026-03-09

**Goal:** Detect and handle frontmatter text fields that contain numeric values, treating them equivalently to native number fields across all analytics, charts, and UI features. Handles the real-world case where YAML format changed over time ŌĆö older entries use `anxiety: 6` (native number) while newer entries use `anxiety: "3"` (quoted string).

### Changes Made

- Added `'numeric-text'` to `FrontmatterField.type` union
- Created `isNumericField(field)` and `getNumericValue(raw)` shared helpers in `FrontmatterService.ts`
- Updated `inferFieldType()` with 80% threshold heuristic that counts both native numbers and parseable numeric strings
- Updated `detectFields()` to compute min/max ranges for numeric-text fields
- Replaced 23+ `f.type === 'number'` filter sites across 3 services and 12 components with `isNumericField(f)`
- Updated badge display in `EntryCard.tsx` to use `getNumericValue()` for polarity coloring
- Updated `settings.ts` polarity and goal field filters to include numeric-text
- Added 21 new tests covering detection, helpers, range computation, and mixed-type scenarios

### Verification
- Ō£ģ 342 tests passing across 25 test files
- Ō£ģ `npm run lint` clean
- Ō£ģ `npm run build` clean
- Ō£ģ Brad manually verified in Obsidian

**`src/components/sidebar/WidgetContainer.tsx`** (~80 lines)

Widget ordering system with **arrow buttons on ALL platforms** (no drag-and-drop ŌĆö avoids interference with Obsidian's workspace drag handlers for tab/leaf management):
- Props: `widgets: { id: string; label: string; component: ReactNode }[]`
- Renders widgets in the order specified by `settings.widgets`
- **Up/down arrow buttons** on each widget header for fine-grained reordering. Arrow buttons must be 44px touch targets. Detected platform via `Platform.isMobile` for styling only (slightly larger buttons on mobile), not for different UX.
- **Overflow menu (three-dot icon)** on each widget header with "Move to top" and "Move to bottom" options. This gives O(1) repositioning for big jumps (moving widget from position 7 to 1 without 6 arrow taps).
- Each widget has a visibility toggle (eye icon) ŌĆö toggling sets `visible: false` in the `widgets` array but preserves the entry for re-enabling later
- On reorder or visibility change: updates `settings.widgets` via `saveSettingsDebounced()` (500ms debounce, see Plan-Wide Rules "Settings Save Debounce"). In-memory state updates immediately for visual feedback.
- **Migration:** Settings migration from previous version converts `widgetOrder: string[]` to `widgets: { id: string; visible: true }[]`.

This makes the scoring system transparent and encourages users to improve their journaling by making the "game" visible.

Task completion tracking from pre-computed checkbox counts:
- Props: `productivitySections: string[]`, `excludedSections: string[]`
- Reads entries from `journalStore` internally
- **Performance:** Does NOT parse section text at render time. Instead, reads `entry.tasksCompleted` and `entry.tasksTotal` (pre-computed during Pass 2 indexing by counting `- [ ]` vs `- [x]` in configured sections). See JournalEntry type additions below.
- Computes "Productivity Score" per entry: `completedCheckboxes / totalCheckboxes * 100`
- Displays:

**`src/utils/taskParser.ts`** (~40 lines)
```typescript
/**
 * Parse markdown content for checkboxes within specified sections.
 * Returns { completed: number, total: number } for each section.
 * Respects productivitySections whitelist and excludedSections blacklist.
 */
/**
 * Whitelist semantics: When `productivitySections` is empty (`[]`), treat it as "all sections" (no whitelist filter).
 * `excludedSections` is always applied as a blacklist on top. This means the feature works out of the box ŌĆö
 * all checkboxes in all sections count toward productivity, minus explicitly excluded sections (default: `['Meds']`).
 */
export function parseTaskCompletion(
    sections: Record<string, string>,
    productivitySections: string[],
    excludedSections: string[]
): { section: string; completed: number; total: number }[]

/**
 * Compute overall productivity score from task completion data.
 * Returns 0-100 percentage, or null if no checkboxes found.
 */
export function computeProductivityScore(
    tasks: { completed: number; total: number }[]
): number | null

/**
 * Reindex trigger: When `productivitySections` or `excludedSections` settings change,
 * trigger a re-parse of `tasksCompleted` and `tasksTotal` for all entries using `processWithYielding()`.
 * This ensures historical task metrics reflect the new configuration.
 * Wire this via a settings change subscription in `main.ts` (same pattern as `metricsCacheStore` staleness wiring).
 */
```

### JournalEntry Type Additions (Phase 6c)

/** Number of completed checkboxes (- [x]) in configured productivity sections */
tasksCompleted: number;
/** Total number of checkboxes (- [ ] + - [x]) in configured productivity sections */
tasksTotal: number;
```
These are computed once during indexing, avoiding re-parsing section text on every render.

**`src/utils/colorThemes.ts`** (~50 lines)

/** Calendar color palette definitions */
export interface ColorTheme {
    name: string;
    /** Maps a 0-1 normalized value to a CSS color string */
    mapValue: (normalized: number) => string;
    /** Color for missing/null values.
     *  Must be a CSS variable reference resolved at render time, NOT a hardcoded hex.
     *  Component resolves via: getComputedStyle(document.body).getPropertyValue('--background-modifier-border').trim()
     *  and passes the resolved value to mapValue(). See Plan-Wide Rules "Color Theme CSS Variables". */
    emptyColor: string;
 **Rename (amendment):** Rename emptyColor to emptyColorVar in the ColorTheme interface. The component resolves the CSS variable via getComputedStyle and passes the resolved color string to mapValue.
}

export const COLOR_THEMES: Record<string, ColorTheme> = {
    default: { /* red -> yellow -> green HSL interpolation (existing) */ },
    monochrome: { /* gray -> navy */ },
    warm: { /* peach -> orange */ },
    cool: { /* cyan -> purple */ },
    colorblind: { /* blue -> orange, viridis-inspired, accessible to ~8% of males with red-green deficiency */ },
};
```

## Phase 7: Actionable Echoes + Lens (~2 sessions) Ō£ģ COMPLETE

**Depends on:** Phase 5b (field polarity, `getPolarityColor()`, `MetricComparison` type). Phase 7's `ActionableEcho` and `CopingLookup` use polarity-aware metric comparison and directional coloring.

**Goal:** Expand echoes from simple "on this day" to rich, data-aware retrospection with metric comparisons and coping lookups. Build the Lens panel for full-text search and compound filtering.

### Pre-Phase Fix: dateIndex stale keys on date change
 **Amendment:** This fix is already implemented in the current codebase (journalStore.ts lines 150-162 and 210-223). Convert this to verification and regression test only. Do NOT re-implement existing working code.

When a user edits their frontmatter `date` field, the entry's date changes but the old `MM-DD` key in `dateIndex` still holds a reference to the entry. Fix `journalStore.upsertEntry()` to detect date changes and update the dateIndex:
```typescript
// In upsertEntry(), before adding the new entry:
const existing = entries.get(entry.filePath);
if (existing) {
    const oldKey = formatMonthDay(existing.date); // "MM-DD"
    const newKey = formatMonthDay(entry.date);
    if (oldKey !== newKey) {
        // Remove from old dateIndex key
        const oldList = dateIndex.get(oldKey);
        if (oldList) {
            const filtered = oldList.filter(e => e.filePath !== entry.filePath);
            if (filtered.length === 0) dateIndex.delete(oldKey);
            else dateIndex.set(oldKey, filtered);
        }
    }
}
```
This fix is retroactive (affects Phase 1 code) but becomes pertinent now because Phase 7 echoes rely heavily on `dateIndex` accuracy.

**Historical corruption cleanup:** The fix above prevents future stale keys, but any entries whose `date` field was edited before this patch may have orphaned `dateIndex` entries. On the first `initialize()` after this patch is deployed, rebuild `dateIndex` from scratch: clear the Map and repopulate it by iterating all entries. This is a one-time O(n) operation during startup. Add regression tests for: "date changed twice in succession" and "stale key cleanup removes orphaned entries."

### Files to Create

**`src/services/EchoesService.ts`** -- Expand with:
```typescript
/**
 * Compare today's metrics with a past echo entry.
 * Returns field-by-field comparison with direction and magnitude.
 * E.g., { field: 'mood', today: 7, then: 3, direction: 'improved', change: +4 }
 * Only compares fields that exist in both entries.
 */
export function compareMetrics(
    todayEntry: JournalEntry | undefined,
    echoEntry: JournalEntry,
    fields: FrontmatterField[],
    polarity: Record<string, string>
): MetricComparison[]

/**
 * "Last time you felt this way" -- find entries where a specific field
 * had a similar value to today (within +/- tolerance).
 * Returns the N most recent matches, excluding today.
 * Includes the entry's section content for coping context.
 */
export function findSimilarEntries(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    fieldKey: string,
    targetValue: number,
    tolerance: number,
    limit?: number
): JournalEntry[]

/**
 * Detect milestone entries.
 * Returns milestones like "100th entry", "1 year of journaling", "365-day streak".
 */
export function detectMilestones(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    currentStreak: number,
    referenceDate: Date
): Milestone[]

/**
 * Get echoes for additional time periods beyond "on this day" and "this week last year":
 * - "This time last month" -- same day of month, previous months
 * - "This time last quarter" -- same relative day, 3/6/9/12 months ago
 */
export function getExtendedEchoes(
    entries: JournalEntry[],
    referenceDate: Date
): { period: string; entries: JournalEntry[] }[]
```
