**`src/components/wizard/WeeklyReviewApp.tsx`** (~90 lines)

Weekly review wizard with pre-populated data:
- **Page 1 -- Week Summary (read-only):**
  - Average mood, energy, sleep, anxiety for the week
  - Meds/workout completion rates
  - Best day and worst day excerpts
  - "Tomorrow's Top 3" entries from each day (cross-reference follow-through)
  - Writing volume, entry count, consistency score
  - Productivity score for the week
- **Page 2 -- Reflections (editable):**
  - "What went well this week?" text area
  - "What could be improved?" text area
  - "Goals for next week" text area
  - Custom text areas for any additional sections the user wants. Custom sections can be persisted as a template via `settings.weeklyReviewCustomSections: string[]` (default `[]`). An "+ Add section" button lets the user type a label and get a text area. A "Save as template" checkbox persists these labels so they auto-appear in future weekly reviews. The generated note includes custom sections as `## headings`. **Limits:** Maximum 10 custom sections (prevent pathological configs). Section name max length: 100 characters. Both enforced at UI level with clear feedback. **Deduplication:** When the user adds a custom section, check `weeklyReviewCustomSections.some(s => s.toLowerCase().trim() === input.toLowerCase().trim())` ŌĆö show a Notice if duplicate.
 **Section label sanitization (amendment):** Sanitize custom section labels by removing leading markdown-active characters (``#``, ``-``, ``*``, ``>``, ``[``, ``]``) and collapsing multiple spaces. Labels like "## Already a heading" or "- [ ] A task" would create malformed markdown when used as ``## headings`` in the generated note.
- **Empty-state handling:** If there are zero entries for the current week, show a descriptive empty state ("No entries found for this week") instead of rendering empty stat cards or crashing.
- "Generate & Save" button: creates a weekly review note in `weeklyReviewFolder`

**`src/utils/sectionUtils.ts`** (~40 lines)

Section content replacement utility for the wizard's body section writes:
```typescript
/**
 * Replace the content of a specific ## section within full note text.
 * Finds the section start (after the `## heading` line), the section end
 * (before the next `##` heading or EOF), and replaces just that section's
 * content while preserving everything before/after.
 *
 * Returns the modified full text. Returns original text unchanged if
 * the heading is not found.
 */
export function replaceSectionContent(
    fullText: string,
    heading: string,
    newContent: string,
    occurrenceIndex?: number  // default 0; for duplicate headings
): string
```
This must handle: headings with emoji, headings inside code blocks (skip them), empty sections (heading immediately followed by another heading), CRLF vs LF line endings, and **duplicate headings** (the `occurrenceIndex` parameter specifies which occurrence to replace, defaulting to 0 for the first). Section boundaries are defined by the next heading **at the same or higher level** ŌĆö a `##` section includes all its `###` and `####` subsections. **IMPORTANT:** Must reuse `SectionParserService`'s code-block-aware heading detection logic ŌĆö do NOT implement a separate regex. This ensures consistency between the parsing used during indexing and the replacement used during editing.
 **CRLF handling (amendment):** Normalize the entire file to LF on save. Obsidian internally uses LF; CRLF files in Obsidian are the exception and typically come from external editors. Document this decision: ``replaceSectionContent()`` normalizes all line endings to LF to prevent mixed line endings when only some sections are modified.
   **Implementation note:** Extract `findSectionBoundaries(text: string): { heading: string; level: number; startIndex: number; endIndex: number; occurrenceIndex: number }[]` from `SectionParserService` as a public utility in `src/utils/sectionUtils.ts` (created in Phase 8a, see Phase 8 sub-phase note). Both `parseSections()` and `replaceSectionContent()` call this internally ŌĆö the code-block-aware heading regex lives in exactly one place. The `level` field tracks heading depth (2 for `##`, 3 for `###`, etc.) and `occurrenceIndex` tracks duplicate headings.

## Phase 12: Time Machine Slider (evaluate after all views)
 **Contextual jump activation (amendment):** Any contextual navigation targeting a historical date (calendar click, echo card click) should activate the Time Machine with that date, creating a cohesive browsing mode.

**Persistent "viewing past" indicator:** When the time machine slider is active (not on today's date), display a thin accent bar at the top of the main view: `­¤ōģ Viewing: January 15, 2025 [Reset to today]`. This prevents confusion when users switch between tabs that respect/ignore the time machine context.

**Goal:** A global date navigation slider that all date-aware components can optionally respond to. Deferred to after all views exist so we can evaluate which components benefit from it and how the UX should work.

**Decision point:** After Phases 5-11 are complete, evaluate:
1. Which views/components would benefit from a global date slider?
2. Should it be a persistent UI element (always visible at the top of the main view)?
3. Or should it be a per-tab control that only appears on date-aware tabs?
4. How does it interact with existing date controls (calendar month nav, date range pickers, period selectors)?

### Tentative Design (to be refined)

**`src/components/shared/TimeMachineSlider.tsx`** (~60 lines)
- `<input type="range">` with min = first entry date, max = last entry date
``input`` event for real-time visual feedback (date label update) and the ``change`` event for committing the value to the store. The ``change`` event fires on mouseup/touchend for range inputs natively. Do NOT use ``setPointerCapture()`` on ``<input type="range">`` ├óŌé¼ŌĆØ it has inconsistent behavior on iOS Safari WebView and can interfere with the browser's built-in slider interaction. Add ``{ passive: true }`` to touch event listeners on the slider to avoid scroll-blocking warnings on mobile. Test the slider on iOS Obsidian specifically.
``timeMachineStore.date``
- Shows formatted date label above the slider thumb
- Optional: play/pause button for auto-advance (step through days at 1 second intervals)
- CSS class: `hindsight-time-machine`

### Time Machine Precedence Rules (define now, implement in Phase 12)

To prevent architectural surprises when building Phase 12, the following precedence rules are established now:

| Component | Time Machine active? | Behavior |
|-----------|---------------------|----------|
| Today tab (sidebar) | Ō£ģ Overrides | Shows data for the slider date instead of today |
| Echoes | Ō£ģ Overrides | Shows "on this day" echoes relative to slider date |
| Morning Briefing | Ō£ģ Overrides | Shows briefing data for slider date |
| Charts date range | ŌØī Doesn't override | User's manually selected range takes precedence |
| Calendar month nav | ŌØī Doesn't override | User's navigated month takes precedence |
| Pulse dashboard | Ō£ģ Overrides | Recalculates stats relative to slider date |
| Lens filters | ŌØī Doesn't override | User's explicit filter criteria take precedence |
| Section Reader | ŌØī Doesn't override | Independent date range control |

**Reset:** A "Reset to today" button on the Time Machine slider clears the override and returns all components to using the actual current date.



**Implementation note:** Phase 12 adds the slider UI and the above override/pass-through logic to each component.

**Note for earlier phases:** Components built in Phases 6b-11 (Morning Briefing, Digest, Quick-Edit, Weekly Review) should read their default date from a hook that can be overridden later. Use `useTimeMachineDate()` (returns `timeMachineDate ?? startOfDay(new Date())`) from Phase 12's store if it exists, or fall back to `startOfDay(new Date())` if Phase 12 hasn't been implemented yet. The precedence matrix above will be expanded to cover Phase 10-11 features (Digest period default, Quick-edit default date, Weekly Review baseline, annotation marker filtering) during Phase 12 planning ŌĆö these don't need to be decided now.
 **Midnight timeout optimization (A18):** Instead of a per-minute `setInterval` that fires 1,440 times/day just to check if the date rolled over, use a **single `setTimeout` that fires at midnight**:
  ```typescript
  function scheduleNextMidnight(callback: () => void): ReturnType<typeof setTimeout> {
      const now = new Date();
      const tomorrow = new Date(now.getFullYear(), now.getMonth(), now.getDate() + 1);
      const msUntilMidnight = tomorrow.getTime() - now.getTime() + 100; // +100ms buffer
      return setTimeout(() => {
          callback();
          scheduleNextMidnight(callback); // chain for the next day
      }, msUntilMidnight);
  }
  ```
  On each midnight tick, update the store's `today` value. The `reset()` action must clear the timeout ID. Register via `plugin.registerInterval()` if possible, otherwise track manually in `cleanupRegistry`. This reduces timer overhead from 1,440 fires/day to 1 fire/day.

### Architecture Notes (decided now to prevent coupling issues)

**Separate store:** Use a dedicated `src/store/timeMachineStore.ts` ŌĆö do NOT add `timeMachineDate` to `uiStore`. Adding it to `uiStore` creates hidden coupling: every component that subscribes to `uiStore` for unrelated state (tab selections, sort order, filters) would need careful selector isolation to avoid re-renders when the slider moves. A separate store makes the opt-in boundary explicit.

```typescript
// src/store/timeMachineStore.ts
interface TimeMachineState {
    /** Active slider date (null = deactivated, use today) */
    date: Date | null;
    setDate: (date: Date | null) => void;
    reset: () => void;
}
```

**Opt-in hook:** Components opt in via a `useTimeMachineDate()` hook that returns `timeMachineDate ?? startOfDay(new Date())`. If the slider isn't active (date is null), the hook returns today's date ŌĆö components don't need branching logic.

**Explicit activate/deactivate toggle:** The slider should have a visible on/off toggle. When deactivated, `date` is `null` and all components fall through to their normal date logic. This prevents confusion about "why does the sidebar show yesterday's data?" after the user forgets the slider is active.

**Performance:** Components must use Zustand selectors (`useTimeMachineStore(s => s.date)`) to subscribe only to the date field. Only the 5 subscribing components update when the slider moves, not the entire view tree. Components that don't use the time machine date (e.g., IndexFilters, TagFrequencyChart) must not subscribe.

### Verification
1. Slider appears in the designated location
2. Dragging slider changes the selected date
3. Subscribing components update to show data for the selected date
4. Release slider (mouseUp/touchEnd) triggers the update (not during drag)
5. "Reset to today" button clears the time machine override
6. Components gracefully handle the transition between "now" and a historical date

## Phase Dependency Graph

```
Phase 0 (Scaffold)
  +-- Phase 1 -> 1.5 (Index Service + Store -> Tests)
      +-- Phase 2 -> 2.5 (Sidebar: Today + Echoes -> Tests)
      +-- Phase 3 -> 3.5 (Full-Page: Calendar -> Tests)
      |   +-- Phase 4 -> 4.5 (Timeline + Index -> Tests)
      +-- Phase 5a (Infrastructure Cleanup + Foundation Utilities)
      |   +-- Phase 5b (Charts + Tab Groups + Sparklines)
      |       +-- Phase 5c (Correlation + Trend Alerts + Polarity)
      |           +-- Phase 5.5 (Chart & Metrics Tests)
      |           +-- Phase 6a (Pulse + Heatmap + Personal Bests)
      |           |   +-- Phase 6b (Goals + Today Tab Enhancements)
      |           |       +-- Phase 6c (Widgets + Themes + Quality)
      |           |           +-- Phase 6.5 (Pulse & Dashboard Tests)
      |           |               +-- Phase 8 -> 8.5 (Threads + Section Reader -> Tests)
      |           +-- Phase 7 -> 7.5 (Actionable Echoes + Lens -> Tests)  *** DEPENDS ON 5c ***
      +-- Phase 9 -> 9.5 (DEPENDS ON: Phase 5a for appStore + Phase 5b for Tab Groups) (Images + Thumbnails + Gallery -> Tests)
      +-- Phase 10 -> 10.5 (Digest + Export + Annotations -> Tests)
      |       +-- Phase 11 -> 11.5 (Quick-Edit + Wizards -> Tests)  *** DEPENDS ON Phase 10 (NoteCreationService) ***
      +-- Phase 12 -> 12.5 (Time Machine -- evaluate after all views -> Tests)
```

> **Note:** Phases 9 and 10 retroactively modify Phase 1-5b code: Phase 9 updates `CalendarCell.tsx` and `EntryCard.tsx` (thumbnail integration). Phase 10 updates `MetricChart.tsx` (annotation markers). These cross-phase modifications are called out in each phase's documentation but are important background for scheduling.

> **Note:** Phase 7 depends on Phase 5c (field polarity, `getPolarityColor()`, `MetricComparison` type) for polarity-aware metric comparison and directional coloring in `ActionableEcho` and `CopingLookup`. If Phase 7 needs to start before 5c, stub polarity to 'neutral' and skip directional coloring.

> **Note:** Phase 9 does NOT depend on Phase 8's `useSharedObserver`. The Gallery uses its own `ResizeObserver` instance for container-level resize detection. Phase 9 depends only on Phase 5a (appStore, yieldUtils) and Phase 5b (Tab Groups for Gallery tab placement). This means Phase 9 can be scheduled in parallel with Phases 6-8 if desired.

> **Note:** Phase 11 depends on Phase 1 (for `detectedFields` and `processFrontMatter`) but is otherwise independent. It benefits from Phase 6 data (goal targets, consistency scores) being available in the wizard, but can be started earlier if needed. Phase 10's `NoteCreationService` is used by Phase 11's wizards, so Phase 10 should complete first.

## Testing Rules (from workflow gates)

1. X.5 testing phases are a **SEPARATE task** from their parent phase
2. **Never** start writing tests until Brad has explicitly confirmed the parent phase works in Obsidian
3. All test output piped to `test-output.txt` per `.agent/workflows/test.md`
4. Tests run with `npx vitest run` -- capture output:
   ```powershell
   npx vitest run 2>&1 | Out-File -Encoding utf8 test-output.txt
   Get-Content test-output.txt -Tail 20
   ```
5. `test-output.txt` is gitignored
6. Clean up with `Remove-Item test-output.txt` when done
